# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the Kafka Streams topology build and compilation process. The answer file includes:

## Summary

**Files Identified** (10 total):
1. **StreamsBuilder.java** - The public DSL API entry point
2. **InternalStreamsBuilder.java** - Graph compilation and optimization
3. **InternalTopologyBuilder.java** - State store registration and physical topology building
4. **ProcessorTopology.java** - The compiled physical topology with processor nodes
5. **StateStoreNode.java** - Graph node that registers state stores
6. **StreamTask.java** - Where processor nodes are initialized for execution
7. **TopologyMetadata.java** - Higher-level orchestration of the build process
8. **Topology.java** - Logical topology container
9. **StoreBuilder.java** - Interface for state store builders
10. **AbstractTask.java** - Base task class

**Key Chain of Execution**:
1. `StreamsBuilder.build()` → initiates the build process
2. `InternalStreamsBuilder.buildAndOptimizeTopology()` → compiles the DSL graph 
3. `StateStoreNode.writeToTopology()` → registers state stores
4. `InternalTopologyBuilder.addStateStore()` → records store registrations
5. `InternalTopologyBuilder.buildTopology()` → creates the physical ProcessorTopology
6. `ProcessorTopology` → contains the compiled ProcessorNodes, SourceNodes, SinkNodes, and StateStores
7. `StreamTask` → initializes and executes the processor nodes

The document provides detailed line references, method signatures, and explanations of how each component contributes to transforming a high-level topology specification into an executable task graph.

This also means that the work\\n188:      * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\\n189:      * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\\n190:      * <p>\\n191:      * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\\n192:      * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\\n193:      * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\\n194:      *\\n195:      * @param topicPattern the pattern to match for topic names\\n196:      * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\\n197:      */\\n198:     public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern) {\\n199:         return stream(topicPattern, Consumed.with(null, null));\\n200:     }\\n201: \\n202:     /**\\n203:      * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic pattern.\\n204:      * The {@code \\\"auto.offset.reset\\\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\\n205:      * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\\n206:      * <p>\\n207:      * If multiple topics are matched by the specified pattern, the created {@link KStream} will read data from all of\\n208:      * them and there is no ordering guarantee between records from different topics. // key must be local (application state is shared over all running Kafka Streams instances)\\n256:      * }</pre>\\n257:      * For non-local keys, a custom RPC mechanism must be implemented using {@link KafkaStreams#metadataForAllStreamsClients()} to\\n258:      * query the value of the key on a parallel running instance of your Kafka Streams application.\\n259:      *\\n260:      * @param topic              the topic name; import java.util.regex.Pattern;\n48: \n49: /**\n50:  * {@code StreamsBuilder} provides the high-level Kafka Streams DSL to specify a Kafka Streams topology.\n51:  *\n52:  * <p>\n53:  * It is a This also means that the work\n188:      * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\n189:      * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\n190:      * <p>\n191:      * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n192:      * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n193:      * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n194:      *\n195:      * @param topicPattern the pattern to match for topic names\n196:      * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\n197:      */\n198:     public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern) {\n199:         return stream(topicPattern, Consumed.with(null, null));\n200:     }\n201: \n202:     /**\n203:      * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic pattern.\n204:      * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n205:      * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n206:      * <p>\n207:      * If multiple topics are matched by the specified pattern, the created {@link KStream} will read data from all of\n208:      * them and there is no ordering guarantee between records from different topics. // key must be local (application state is shared over all running Kafka Streams instances)\n256:      * }</pre>\n257:      * For non-local keys, a custom RPC mechanism must be implemented using {@link KafkaStreams#metadataForAllStreamsClients()} to\n258:      * query the value of the key on a parallel running instance of your Kafka Streams application.\n259:      *\n260:      * @param topic              the topic name;
